### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is worth 0.
  We need to find the value of the equipment 4 years after it is purchased.
  
Action: 

Let's use straight-line depreciation to calculate the value of the equipment after 4 years.

The depreciation per year is $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700$.

After 4 years, the equipment will have depreciated by $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$.

The value of the equipment after 4 years is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.

Therefore, the answer is (C) $\$ 21,600$.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  To find the depreciation rate, we divide the initial value by the number of years it depreciates.
  The depreciation expense is the depreciation rate times the number of years.
  The book value of the equipment after a certain number of years is the initial value minus the depreciation expense times the number of years.
Action: 
  The depreciation rate is $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12}= \$ 2,700$ per year.
  The depreciation expense after 4 years is $4 \times \$ 2,700 = \$ 10,800$.
  The book value after 4 years is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.
  Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, it is considered to have no monetary value.
Action: 
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years, so each year it loses the same amount of value. 
  Let's call this amount "x". 
  After 12 years, the equipment has lost a total of $12x$ value.
  Since the equipment is worth $\$32,400$ initially, its value after 4 years would be:
  $\$32,400 - 4x$
  We can find "x" by dividing the total depreciation by the number of years:
  $12x = \$32,400 - \$0$
  $x = \$2,700$
  So, the value of the equipment after 4 years is:
  $\$32,400 - 4x = \$32,400 - 4(\$2,700) = \$21,600$
  Answer: Choice (C) $\$21,600$
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  The depreciation rate is constant, which means it decreases at the same rate every year.
  
Solution:
  Since the depreciation rate is constant, we can divide the total depreciation by the number of years to obtain the annual depreciation rate.
  The total depreciation is the initial value minus the final value, which is zero.
  So, the annual depreciation rate is $\frac{\$32,400}{12}= \$2,700$.
  Therefore, the value of the camera equipment after 4 years is $\$32,400 - 4(\$2,700) = \$21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Knowledge: 
  If an asset depreciates at a constant rate, its value decreases linearly over time.
  To find the rate of depreciation, we can divide the total depreciation by the number of years of useful life.
  Once we have the rate of depreciation, we can find the value of the asset at any point in time using the formula: value = original value - (rate of depreciation) * (time since purchase).
  In this case, the useful life of the camera equipment is 12 years, and its total depreciation is $\$ 32,400$, so its rate of depreciation is $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12 \text{ years}} = \$ 2,700/\text{year}$.
Action: Answer("B")  

To find the value of the camera equipment 4 years after it is purchased, we can use the formula:

value = original value - (rate of depreciation) * (time since purchase)

value = $\$ 32,400 - (\$ 2,700/\text{year}) * (4 \text{ years})$

value = $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800$

value = $\$ 21,600$

Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ 4 years after it is purchased. The answer is (C) $\$ 21,600$.

Response 6:
Knowledge:
  The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  We want to find the value of the equipment 4 years after it is purchased.
  
Solution:
  Since the equipment depreciates at a constant rate, we can model its value as a linear function of time. Let $V(t)$ be the value of the equipment $t$ years after it is purchased, where $t$ is measured in years. We know that $V(0) = 32,400$ and $V(12) = 0$. Therefore, the slope of the line connecting these two points is:
  
  $$m = \frac{V(12)-V(0)}{12-0} = \frac{0-32,400}{12} = -2,700$$
  
  So the equation of the line is:
  
  $$V(t) = -2,700t + 32,400$$
  
  To find the value of the equipment 4 years after it is purchased, we plug in $t=4$:
  
  $$V(4) = -2,700(4) + 32,400 = 20,400$$
  
  Therefore, the equipment is worth $\$ 20,400$ 4 years after it is purchased.
  
Action: Answer("C")

Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We can start by multiplying both sides of the equation by a, which is negative. When we multiply by a negative number, we need to reverse the inequality signs.
  A: If $c>1$, then $(a-b)/a > 1$, which implies that $a-b > a$, which is not possible if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive.
  B: If $c=1$, then $(a-b)/a = 1$, which implies that $a-b = a$, which is not possible if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive.
  C: If $c=-1$, then $(a-b)/a = -1$, which implies that $a-b = -a$. Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $a-b$ is negative and $-a$ is positive. Therefore, this equation can be satisfied.
  D: If $c<-1$, then $(a-b)/a < -1$, which implies that $a-b < -a$, which is not possible if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive.

Action:

Therefore, $h(5)-h(3)=32-8=24$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The volume of a cylinder is given by $V = Bh$ where $B$ is the area of the base and $h$ is the height of the cylinder.
  The total volume of the can containing fruit and syrup is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  We can find the volume of the syrup by subtracting the volume of the fruit from the total volume of the can.
  We can find the volume of the fruit by subtracting the volume of the syrup from the volume of the can.
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ is too small compared to the other options.
  B: To find the volume of the fruit, we need to subtract the volume of the syrup from the total volume of the can. The volume of the can is $V = Bh = 75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2} \cdot 10 \mathrm{~cm} = 750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$. Therefore, the volume of the fruit is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$. This matches choice C.
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ is the correct answer.
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ is the volume of the can, not the volume of the fruit.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:

Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\2 y-x=-19\end{array}$$What is the solution $(x, y)$ to the system of equations above?
Choices:
  A: $(-5,-2)$
  B: $(3,-8)$
  C: $(4,-6)$
  D: $(9,-6)$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve the system of equations, we can use substitution or elimination method.
  Let's use the elimination method:
  Multiplying the second equation by 3 and adding it to the first equation, we get:
  $$3x+4y-3(2y-x)=-23-3(-19)$$
  which simplifies to:
  $$6x-2y=34 \quad \Rightarrow \quad 3x-y=17$$
  Now, multiplying the second equation by 4 and adding it to the first equation, we get:
  $$3x+4y+4(2y-x)=-23+4(-19)$$
  which simplifies to:
  $$-5x=-95 \quad \Rightarrow \quad x=19$$
  Substituting the value of $x$ in the equation $3x-y=17$, we get:
  $$3(19)-y=17 \quad \Rightarrow \quad y=-2$$
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: To solve this system of equations, we can use the elimination method or substitution method. Let's use the substitution method. We can solve for $x$ in the second equation and substitute into the first equation to solve for $y$. Then we can substitute the value of $y$ back into either equation to solve for $x$.

$$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\2 y-x=-19\end{array}$$

Solving the second equation for $x$:

$$\begin{align}2y-x&=-19\\x&=2y+19\end{align}$$

Substituting $x$ into the first equation:

$$\begin{align}3(2y+19)+4y&=-23\\6y+57+4y&=-23\\10y&=-80\\y&=-8\end{align}$$

Substituting $y$ back into the second equation to solve for $x$:

$$\begin{align}2(-8)-x&=-19\\-16-x&=-19\\x&=-3\end{align}$$

Therefore, the solution to the system of equations is $(x,y)=(-3,-8)$.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  To solve a system of two equations with two unknowns, we need to find the values of $x$ and $y$ that satisfy both equations simultaneously.
  We can solve the system by using the substitution method or elimination method.

Substitution method:
  Solve one equation for one variable and substitute the expression into the other equation.
  $2y-x=-19$ can be rearranged as $x=2y+19$.
  Substitute $x=2y+19$ into $3x+4y=-23$:
  $3(2y+19)+4y=-23$
  $10y+57=-23$
  $10y=-80$
  $y=-8$
  Substitute $y=-8$ into $x=2y+19$:
  $x=2(-8)+19$
  $x=3$
  Therefore, the solution is $(x,y)=(3,-8)$.

Elimination method:
  Multiply the first equation by 2 and add it to the second equation to eliminate $x$.
  $6x+8y=-46$
  $-6x+2y=-38$
  Add the two equations:
  $10y=-84$
  $y=-8$
  Substitute $y=-8$ into the first equation:
  $3x+4(-8)=-23$
  $3x=-9$
  $x=3$
  Therefore, the solution is $(x,y)=(3,-8)$.

Context: $$.a=1,052+1.08 t.$$.The speed of a sound wave in air depends on the air temperature. The formula above shows the relationship between $a$, the speed of a sound wave, in feet per second, and $t$, the air temperature, in degrees Fahrenheit $\left({ }^{\circ} \mathrm{F}\right)$.
Question: Which of the following expresses the air temperature in terms of the speed of a sound wave?
Choices:
  A: $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$
  B: $t=\frac{a+1,052}{1.08}$
  C: $t=\frac{1,052-a}{1.08}$
  D: $t=\frac{1.08}{a+1,052}$

  To express the air temperature in terms of the speed of sound wave, we need to isolate $t$ on one side of the equation.
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  Subtracting 1,052 from both sides of the equation gives $a - 1,052 = 1.08 t$.
  Dividing both sides by 1.08 gives $t = \frac{a - 1,052}{1.08}$. Therefore, the answer is (A).

Question: If $2 w+4 t=14$ and $4 w+5 t=25$, what is the value of $2 w+3 t ?$
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 10
  C: 13
  D: 17
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  We can solve the system of equations to find the values of $w$ and $t$ and then use them to calculate $2w+3t$.
  One method to solve this system of equations is to use elimination or substitution.
  We can multiply the first equation by $-2$ and add it to the second equation to eliminate $w$ and solve for $t$.
  Then, we can substitute the value of $t$ into one of the original equations to solve for $w$.
  
Action: 
  Multiply the first equation by $-2$ and add it to the second equation to eliminate $w$:
  $$
  \begin{aligned} (-2)(2 w+4 t)+4 w+5 t&=(-2) \cdot 14+25 \\ -4 w-8 t+4 w+5 t&=-28+25 \\ -3 t&=-3 \\ t&=1 \end{aligned}
  $$
  Substitute $t=1$ into the first equation to solve for $w$:
  $$
  \begin{aligned} 2 w+4(1)&=14 \\ 2 w&=10 \\ w&=5 \end{aligned}
  $$
  Calculate $2w+3t$:
  $$
  \begin{aligned} 2 w+3 t &= 2(5)+3(1) \\ &= 10+3 \\ &= 13 \end{aligned}
  $$
  Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We are given two equations, which we can solve for $w$ and $t$.
  Then we can substitute those values into $2w+3t$ to find the answer.
Action: 
  Solve the first equation for $w$: $2w = 14 - 4t \Rightarrow w = 7 - 2t$
  Substitute $w$ into the second equation: $4(7-2t) + 5t = 25 \Rightarrow 28 - 3t = 25 \Rightarrow t = 1$
  Substitute $t=1$ into $w=7-2t$: $w = 7 - 2(1) = 5$
  Substitute $w=5$ and $t=1$ into $2w+3t$: $2(5) + 3(1) = 10 + 3 = 13$
  Answer: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: To find the value of $2w+3t$, we can use the given equations to solve for $w$ and $t$ and then substitute the values in the expression $2w+3t$.
Action: We can solve for $w$ and $t$ as follows:
\begin{align*}
4w+5t &= 25 &&\quad\text{(Given)} \\
2w+4t &= 14 &&\quad\text{(Given)} \\
\Rightarrow 2w+t &= 11 &&\quad\text{(Subtracting the second equation from the first)} \\
\Rightarrow t &= 11-2w &&\quad\text{(Solving for } t \text{ in terms of } w\text{)} \\
\Rightarrow 2w+4(11-2w) &= 14 &&\quad\text{(Substituting } t = 11-2w) \\
\Rightarrow -6w &= -30 &&\quad\text{(Simplifying)} \\
\Rightarrow w &= 5 &&\quad\text{(Dividing both sides by } -6\text{)} \\
\Rightarrow t &= 11-2(5) = 1 &&\quad\text{(Substituting } w=5\text{ in } t = 11-2w) \\
\Rightarrow 2w+3t &= 2(5) + 3(1) = 13 &&\quad\text{(Substituting } w=5\text{ and } t=1\text{ in } 2w+3t) \\
Answer: Answer("C")

Question: $$3 x+x+x+x-3-2=7+x+x$$In the equation above, what is the value of $x$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-\frac{5}{7}$
  B: 1
  C: $\frac{12}{7}$
  D: 3
Response 0:
Action: Answer("C")

Knowledge:
We can solve the equation by simplifying and isolating $x$ on one side of the equation.
We start by combining like terms on both sides of the equation:
$$3x+x+x+x-3-2=7+x+x$$
Simplifying the left side:
$$6x-5=2x+7$$
We isolate $x$ on one side by subtracting $2x$ from both sides:
$$6x-2x-5=7$$
Simplifying:
$$4x=12$$
Dividing by 4 on both sides, we get:
$$x=\frac{12}{4}=\frac{3}{1}=3$$

Therefore, the answer is D, 3.

Question: $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$The equation above is true for all $x$, where $a$ and $b$ are constants. What is the value of $a b$ ?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 20
  C: 24
  D: 40
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The equation above is equivalent to $5ax^{3}+(12-5b)x^{2}+(12-4ab)x+12=20x^{3}-9x^{2}-2x+12$.
  Two polynomials are equal for all $x$ if and only if their corresponding coefficients are equal.
Action: 
  Equating the coefficients of $x^{3}$ gives $5a=20$, which implies $a=4$.
  Equating the coefficients of $x^{2}$ gives $12-5b=-9$, which implies $b=3$.
  Then, $ab=4\cdot3=12$.
  Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  We can start by expanding the left-hand side of the equation and then compare its coefficients to the coefficients of the right-hand side to obtain a system of equations for $a$ and $b$.
  Alternatively, we can use the fact that the equation is true for all $x$ to choose a convenient value of $x$ that simplifies the equation and allows us to solve for $a$ and $b$.
  We can choose $x=0$ to obtain $3\cdot 4=12$, which implies that $a=1$.
  Then, we can choose $x=1$ to obtain $8-3b=20$, which implies that $b=-4$.

  We can expand the left side of the equation and compare the coefficients of each term with the coefficients of the right side of the equation to solve for $a$ and $b$.

$$5a x^3+(12-5b) x^2 + (12-4ab) x + 12a = 20x^3 - 9x^2 - 2x + 12$$
Comparing the coefficients of each term on both sides gives the following system of equations:
$$\begin{aligned}5a &= 20 \\12-5b &= -9 \\ 12-4ab &= -2 \\ 12a &= 12\end{aligned}$$
Solving this system of equations gives $a=4$ and $b=-3$. Therefore, $ab=4(-3)=-12$.

For the coefficient of $x^3$: 
$20a=20 \Rightarrow a=1$

For the coefficient of $x^2$: 
$11x^2(5a-3b)= -9x^2 \Rightarrow 11(5-3b)=-9 \Rightarrow b=8/3$

Finally, we can calculate the product of $a$ and $b$: 
$ab=1\times\frac{8}{3}=\frac{8}{3}$

Question: For $i=\sqrt{-1}$, what is the sum $(7+3 i)+(-8+9 i) ?$
Choices:
  A: $-1+12 i$
  B: $-1-6 i$
  C: $15+12 i$
  D: $15-6 i$ 3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The sum of two complex numbers is found by adding the real parts and adding the imaginary parts separately.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To add complex numbers, we add their real parts and their imaginary parts separately.
  $i = \sqrt{-1}$ is the imaginary unit.
  
Action: Answer("B") 

$(7+3i)+(-8+9i) = (7-8)+(3i+9i) = -1+12i$ 

Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ -1-6i}$.
Response 2:

  For $a+bi$ and $c+di$, the sum is $(a+c)+(b+d)i$.

Hence, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ -1-6i}$.

Question: If $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$, which of the following is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ ?
Choices:
  A: $(a+2 b)^{2}$
  B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
  C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$
  D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We can expand the expression $4z+8y$ as $4(a^2+b^2)+8(ab)$.
  We can factor $a^2+b^2$ as $(a+b)^2-2ab$.
  We can also factor $2ab$ as $2ab$.
  By substituting these factorizations, we get $4(a^2+b^2)+8(ab)=4[(a+b)^2-2ab]+8(2ab)$, which simplifies to $4(a+b)^2$.
  A: $(a+2b)^2$ is equivalent to $a^2+4ab+4b^2$, which is not equal to $4(a+b)^2$.
  B: $(2a+2b)^2$ is equivalent to $4a^2+8ab+4b^2$, which is not equal to $4(a+b)^2$.
  C: $(4a+4b)^2$ is equivalent to $16a^2+32ab+16b^2$, which is not equal to $4(a+b)^2$.
  D: $(4a+8b)^2$ is equivalent to $16a^2+64ab+64b^2$, which is not equal to $4(a+b)^2$.
Action: Answer("A")

B: $(2a+2b)^2$ is equivalent to $4(a^{2}+2ab+b^{2})$.
C: $(4a+4b)^2$ is equivalent to $16a^{2}+32ab+16b^{2}$.
D: $(4a+8b)^{2}$ is equivalent to $16a^{2}+64ab+64b^{2}$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 16 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise is linear.
  A linear function has the form of $f(x) = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The y-intercept represents the shipping charge when the weight of the merchandise is 0.
  We can use the given data to find the slope and y-intercept of the linear function.
  
Slope: 
  We can use any two data points to find the slope.
  Let's use the points $(5, 16.94)$ and $(10, 21.89)$.
  slope $m = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1} = \frac{21.89 - 16.94}{10 - 5} = 0.99$
  
Y-intercept: 
  We can use any data point and the slope to find the y-intercept.
  Let's use the point $(5, 16.94)$.
  y-intercept $b = y - mx = 16.94 - 0.99 \cdot 5 = 11.99$
  
Therefore, the function that represents the shipping charge $f(x)$ for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds is:
  $f(x) = 0.99x + 11.99$
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise, so the function that models this relationship should be in the form of $f(x)=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept. 
  According to the table, when the weight of merchandise increases by 5 pounds, the shipping charge increases by $4.95. Therefore, the slope of the function is $4.95/5=0.99$. 
  When the weight of merchandise is 0, the shipping charge is $16.94$, which gives us the y-intercept of the function. 
Action: Answer("B")  
The function that models the relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise is $f(x)=0.99x+11.99$.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The table shows a linear relationship between the merchandise weight and the shipping charge.
  A linear function has the form $f(x) = mx + b$, where $m$ is the slope of the line and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The y-intercept represents the value of $f(x)$ when $x=0$.
  
To determine the function, we need to find the slope and the y-intercept from the table. 

Using the two points $(5,16.94)$ and $(40,51.59)$, we can find the slope:
$$m = \frac{51.59-16.94}{40-5} = 0.99$$

The y-intercept can be found by substituting one of the points and solving for $b$. Using the point $(5,16.94)$:
$$16.94 = 0.99(5) + b \Rightarrow b = 11.99$$

So the function that represents the relationship between the merchandise weight and the shipping charge is:
$$f(x) = 0.99x + 11.99$$

Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  The table shows a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. 
  The linear equation should be in the form of $y=mx+b$, where $y$ is the dependent variable (shipping charge), $x$ is the independent variable (merchandise weight), $m$ is the slope of the line, and $b$ is the y-intercept of the line. 

To determine the function that relates the shipping charge to the weight of the merchandise, we need to find the slope and y-intercept of the line that passes through the given points. 

We can use the formula for the slope of a line that passes through two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$: 

$$m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$$ 

Let's choose two points from the table: $(5,16.94)$ and $(10,21.89)$. 

$$m=\frac{21.89-16.94}{10-5}=\frac{4.95}{5}=0.99$$ 

Now we can use the point-slope form of the equation of a line to find the y-intercept. We can use the point $(5,16.94)$ and the slope we just found: 

$$y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$$ 
$$y-16.94=0.99(x-5)$$ 

Simplifying: 

$$y=0.99x+11.99$$ 

Action: Answer("B")

Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& \text { Mosteller's formula: } A=\frac{\sqrt{h w}}{60} \\.& \text { Current's formula: } A=\frac{4+w}{30}.\end{aligned}.$$.The formulas above are used in medicine to estimate the body surface area $A$, in square meters, of infants and children whose weight $w$ ranges between 3 and 30 kilograms and whose height $h$ is measured in centimeters.
Question: Based on Current's formula, what is $w$ in terms of $A$ ?
Choices:
  A: $w=30 A-4$
  B: $w=30 A+4$
  C: $w=30(A-4)$
  D: $w=30(A+4)$
Response 0:
Knowledge: The formula given is $A=\frac{4+w}{30}$ and we are asked to solve for $w$ in terms of $A$.
Action: 
$$\begin{aligned}
A &=\frac{4+w}{30} \\
30 A &=4+w \\
w &=30 A-4
\end{aligned}$$
Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(A) } w=30 A-4}$
Response 1:
We need to isolate $w$ in terms of $A$ using the Current's formula. 

$$A=\frac{4+w}{30}$$

$$A=\frac{4}{30}+\frac{w}{30}$$

$$A=\frac{1}{15}+\frac{w}{30}$$

$$A-\frac{1}{15}=\frac{w}{30}$$

$$w=30\left(A-\frac{1}{15}\right)$$

$$w=30A-2$$

Therefore, the answer is A: $w=30 A-4$.

Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, then the relationship can be expressed as $y=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  The slope of a line can be calculated as $\frac{\text{rise}}{\text{run}}=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}$, where $\Delta y$ is the change in y and $\Delta x$ is the change in x between any two points on the line.

Solution:
  We can calculate the slope of the line between the first two points as $\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{-a-0}{3a-a}=-\frac{a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$. We can also calculate the slope of the line between the last two points as $\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{-2a+ a}{5a-3a}=-\frac{a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$. Since both slopes are equal, we can conclude that there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$.
  
  To find the equation of the line, we can use the point-slope form of a line $y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$, where $m$ is the slope and $(x_1,y_1)$ is a point on the line. We can use the point $(a, -a)$, which is on the line, and the slope $-\frac{1}{2}$, which we calculated earlier, to find the equation of the line. 

  Plugging in the values, we get:
  \begin{align*}
  y-(-a)&=-\frac{1}{2}(x-a)\\
  y+a&=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{1}{2}a\\
  y&=-\frac{1}{2}x-\frac{1}{2}a
  \end{align*}

  We can simplify this equation by multiplying both sides by $-2$ to get $2y=x+a$. This equation matches choice $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ x+2y=a}$. 

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  We can find the slope of the line by taking any two points on the line and using the formula $m = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}$.
  Once we have the slope $m$, we can find the $y$-intercept $b$ by using the formula $b = y - mx$ for any point on the line.

Action:

$b = y - mx = 0 - (-\frac{1}{2})a = \frac{1}{2}a$

Therefore, the answer is (B) $x+2y=5a$.

The slope of the line passing through $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$ is $m=\dfrac{-2a+a}{5a-3a}=-\dfrac{a}{2a}=-\dfrac{1}{2}$.

The equation of the line passing through $(3a,-a)$ and $(5a,-2a)$ is $y+a=-\dfrac{1}{2}(x-3a)$, which simplifies to $y=-\dfrac{1}{2}x+\dfrac{5}{2}a$.

Therefore, the equation of the line that represents the linear relationship between $x$ and $y$ is obtained by combining the two equations above: $y=-\dfrac{1}{2}x+\dfrac{1}{2}a$ for $a \leq x \leq 3a$, and $y=-\dfrac{1}{2}x+\dfrac{5}{2}a$ for $3a \leq x \leq 5a$.

Simplifying this equation gives $2y=-x+a$ for $a \leq x \leq 3a$, and $2y=-x+5a$ for $3a \leq x \leq 5a$.

Multiplying the first equation by 2 gives $4y=-2x+2a$, and adding this to the second equation gives $6y=3a \Rightarrow y=\dfrac{1}{2}a$.

Substituting $y=\dfrac{1}{2}a$ into the first equation gives $2(\dfrac{1}{2}a)=-x+a \Rightarrow x=0$.

Therefore, the equation that represents the linear relationship between $x$ and $y$ is $x+2y=a$ for $a \leq x \leq 3a$, and $x+2y=5a$ for $3a \leq x \leq 5a$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 19 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}1 \text { decagram } & =10 \text { grams } \\1,000 \text { milligrams } & =1 \text { gram }\end{aligned}$$A hospital stores one type of medicine in 2-decagram containers. Based on the information given in the box above, how many 1-milligram doses are there in one 2-decagram container?
Choices:
  A: $\quad 0.002$
  B: $\quad 200$
  C: $\quad 2,000$
  D: 20,000
Response 0:
We have $1 \text{ decagram} = 10 \text{ grams} = 10 \cdot 1000 \text{ milligrams} = 10^4 \text{ milligrams}$.
So, $2 \text{ decagrams} = 2 \cdot 10^4 \text{ milligrams}$.
Since there are $1,000$ milligrams in one gram, there are $1,000$ doses of $1$ milligram in $1$ gram.
Therefore, there are $2 \cdot 10^4 \div 1,000 = 20$ doses of $1$ milligram in one 2-decagram container.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
1 decagram = 10 grams

2 decagrams = 20 grams

1 gram = 1000 milligrams

20 grams = 20 * 1000 milligrams = 20,000 milligrams

If there are 20,000 milligrams in one 2-decagram container, and we want to know the number of 1-milligram doses, we can divide 20,000 by 1 to get the answer.

Action: Answer("D") 20,000
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  $1$ decagram $= 10$ grams
  $1,000$ milligrams $= 1$ gram
  $1$ decagram $= 100$ grams
  $1$ gram $= 1,000$ milligrams
  
To solve the problem, we need to convert decagrams to milligrams. We can do this by using the equivalences given in the problem. 

$$\begin{aligned} 2 \text{ decagrams } &= 2 \times 10^1 \text{ grams }\\
&= 2 \times 10^1 \times 10^3 \text{ milligrams }\\
&= 2 \times 10^4 \text{ milligrams } \end{aligned}$$

So there are 2 $\times$ 10$^4$ milligrams in one 2-decagram container.

  A: Its minimum occurs at $(-3, a)$.
  B: Its minimum occurs at $(3, a)$.
  C: Its maximum occurs at $(-3, a)$.
  D: Its maximum occurs at $(3, a)$.

  The vertex of the parabola $y=-(x-h)^2+k$ is at $(h, k)$.

  When the coefficient of the squared term is negative, the parabola opens downwards and the vertex is a maximum point.
  When the coefficient of the squared term is positive, the parabola opens upwards and the vertex is a minimum point.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A psychologist set up an experiment to study the tendency of a person to select the first item when presented with a series of items. In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let $x$ be the number of people who chose the first picture in the entire group of 300 people. Then $36$ out of the first 150 people chose the first picture, and $x-36$ out of the remaining 150 people chose the first picture.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:

Question: Which of the following is an equivalent form of $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) ?$
Choices:
  A: $-2.2 x^{2}+1.6$
  B: $-2.2 x^{2}+11.2$
  C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
  D: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
We can expand $(1.5x-2.4)^2$ and simplify the expression by multiplying $-1$ to each term of $(5.2x^2-6.4)$
$(a-b)^2 = a^2-2ab+b^2$
$-1 \times (5.2x^2-6.4) = -5.2x^2+6.4$
$(1.5x-2.4)^2 = 2.25x^2-7.2x+5.76$
Action: Answer("D")  
Expanding $(1.5x-2.4)^2$ and simplifying $-1 \times (5.2x^2-6.4)$, we get
$$(1.5x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2x^{2}-6.4\right) = (2.25x^2-7.2x+5.76) - (-5.2x^2+6.4) = -2.95x^2-7.2x+0.64$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(D)}}$.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  $(a+b)^2 = a^2 + 2ab + b^2$
  $(a-b)^2 = a^2 - 2ab + b^2$
Action: 

We can start by expanding the first term in the expression as follows:
$$(1.5 x-2.4)^{2} = (1.5x)^2 - 2(1.5x)(2.4) + (2.4)^2$$
$$= 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76$$

Expanding the second term:
$$\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) = 5.2x^2 - 6.4$$

Substituting these values back into the original expression:
$$(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) = (2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76) - (5.2x^2 - 6.4)$$
$$= -2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$$

Therefore, the answer is (D) $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
To solve this problem, we need to use the formula:
$$(a-b)^2 = a^2 - 2ab + b^2$$
where $a = 1.5x$ and $b = 2.4$.
We also need to distribute the negative sign in front of the second expression.

Action: Answer("B")  
Expanding the first expression, we get:
$$(1.5x - 2.4)^2 = (1.5x)^2 - 2(1.5x)(2.4) + 2.4^2 = 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76$$
Distributing the negative sign in front of the second expression, we get:
$$-(5.2x^2 - 6.4) = -5.2x^2 + 6.4$$
Putting the two expressions together, we get:
$$(1.5x - 2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) = 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4 = -2.95x^2 - 7.2x + 11.16$$
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ -2.2 x^{2}+11.2}$.

  Distributive property of multiplication over addition: $a(b+c) = ab + ac$
Action: Answer("D")

Simplifying further we get $2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4 = -2.95x^2 - 7.2x + 12.16.$

Topic: Math
Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A point $(a,b)$ is on the line passing through $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ if and only if $\frac{b-y_1}{a-x_1} = \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
  The line passing through $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ has the equation $y-k = \frac{32-k}{k-2}(x-2)$.
  For the line to pass through the origin, we need $k=64/5$.
  A: When $k=0$, the line does not pass through the origin.
  B: When $k=4$, the line does not pass through the origin.
  C: When $k=8$, the line passes through the origin.
  D: When $k=16$, the line does not pass through the origin.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A line passing through two points $(x_1, y_1), (x_2, y_2)$ can be represented by the equation $y - y_1 = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}(x - x_1)$.
  If a line passes through the origin, then it contains the point $(0,0)$.
  For the line passing through $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$, its equation can be written as $y - k = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(x - 2)$.
Action: 
  To find the value of $k$ that makes the line pass through the origin, we set $x = y = 0$ in the equation above and solve for $k$:
  $0 - k = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(0 - 2) \implies -k = \frac{32 - k}{k - 2}(-2)$
  $\implies k = \frac{64 - 2k}{k - 2} \implies k^2 - 2k = 64 - 2k \implies k^2 = 64 \implies k = \pm 8$.
  Therefore, the possible values of $k$ are $k = \pm 8$.
  Among the choices, only $\textbf{(C)}$ is a possible value of $k$. 
Answer("C")
Response 2:

  \frac{y-y_1}{x-x_1}=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}
  $$
  A: If $k=0$, then the points are $(2,0)$ and $(0,32)$. The equation of the line is:

  $$

Action: Answer("C")
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  A line that passes through the origin has equation $y = mx$ where $m$ is the slope of the line.
  The slope of a line passing through two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ is given by $m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$
  If the line determined by the points $(2,k)$ and $(k,32)$ passes through the origin, then $(0,0)$ is also a point on the line.
  Therefore, the slope of the line is $\frac{32-0}{k-2} = \frac{k-0}{2-k}$
  Cross-multiplying, we get $32(k-2) = k(2-k)$
  Simplifying, we get $k^2 - 34k + 64 = 0$
  This is a quadratic equation in $k$, and we can solve for $k$ using the quadratic formula: $k=\frac{-b\pm\sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2a}$ where $a=1$, $b=-34$, and $c=64$.
  The discriminant $b^2-4ac$ must be non-negative for the equation to have real solutions.
Action: Answer("C")  
  Solving for $k$ using the quadratic formula, we get $k=\frac{34\pm\sqrt{(-34)^2-4(1)(64)}}{2(1)} = \frac{34\pm\sqrt{676-256}}{2} = \frac{34\pm\sqrt{420}}{2}$
  Simplifying, we get $k=17\pm\sqrt{105}$
  Therefore, $k$ could be $8$, which is choice (C).

Question: If 50 one-cent coins were stacked on top of each other in a column, the column would be approximately $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches tall. At this rate, which of the following is closest to the number of one-cent coins it would take to make an 8-inch-tall column?
Choices:
  A: 75
  B: 100
  C: 200
  D: 390
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The height of a stack of coins is directly proportional to the number of coins in the stack.
  If 50 one-cent coins make a $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inch stack, then one one-cent coin is approximately $\frac{3 \frac{7}{8}}{50} = \frac{15}{8 \cdot 50}$ inches tall.
  To find out how many coins are needed to make an 8-inch stack, we can divide 8 by the height of one coin and round to the nearest whole number.
  A: $\frac{8}{\frac{15}{8 \cdot 50}} \approx 53.33$, which rounded to the nearest whole number is 53. This is not close to any of the answer choices.
  B: $\frac{8}{\frac{15}{8 \cdot 50}} \approx 53.33$, which rounded to the nearest whole number is 53. This is also not close to any of the answer choices.
  C: $\frac{8}{\frac{15}{8 \cdot 50}} \approx 106.67$, which rounded to the nearest whole number is 107. This is closest to answer choice C.
  D: $\frac{8}{\frac{15}{8 \cdot 50}} \approx 208.33$, which rounded to the nearest whole number is 208. This is not close to any of the answer choices.

  $\frac{50\ coins}{3\frac{7}{8}\ inches} = \frac{x\ coins}{8\ inches}$

Question: Percent of Residents Who Earned a Bachelor's Degree or Higher\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hlineState & Percent of residents \\\hlineState A & $21.9 \%$ \\\hlineState B & $27.9 \%$ \\\hlineState C & $25.9 \%$ \\\hlineState D & $19.5 \%$ \\\hlineState E & $30.1 \%$ \\\hlineState F & $36.4 \%$ \\\hlineState G & $35.5 \%$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}A survey was given to residents of all 50 states asking if they had earned a bachelor's degree or higher.The results from 7 of the states are given in the table above. The median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for all 50 states was $26.95 \%$. What is the difference between the median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for these 7 states and the median for all 50 states?
Choices:
  A: $0.05 \%$
  B: $0.95 \%$
  C: $1.22 \%$
  D: $7.45 \%$
Response 0:
To find the median of the 7 states, we need to arrange the data in order from least to greatest: 

$19.5 \%$, $21.9 \%$, $25.9 \%$, $27.9 \%$, $30.1 \%$, $35.5 \%$, $36.4 \%$

The median is the middle number, or the average of the two middle numbers. Since we have an odd number of data points, the median is the fourth data point which is $27.9 \%$. 

To find the difference between the median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for these 7 states and the median for all 50 states, we subtract the median of the 7 states from the median of all 50 states: 

$26.95 \% - 27.9 \% = -0.95 \%$

The difference is $-0.95 \%$, which is approximately equal to $-1 \%$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 30 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{c|c}Year & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Subscriptions } \\ \text { sold }\end{array}$ \\\hline2012 & 5,600 \\2013 & 5,880 \\\end{tabular}\end{center}The manager of an online news service received the report above on the number of subscriptions sold by the service. The manager estimated that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 would be double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014 . How many subscriptions did the manager expect would be sold in 2014 ?
Choices:
  A: 6,020
  B: 6,027
  C: 6,440
  D: 6,468 DIRECTIONS
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's call the number of subscriptions sold in 2012 "x". Then, we know that x = 5,600.
  We also know that the number of subscriptions sold in 2013 is 5,880.
  Let's call the number of subscriptions sold in 2014 "y".
  We need to find the value of "y".
  The percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is (5,880 - 5,600)/5,600 = 0.05.
  The percent increase from 2013 to 2014 is (y - 5,880)/5,880.
  The manager estimated that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 would be double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. This means that:
  0.05 = 2((y - 5,880)/5,880 - 0)
Action: 
  Let's first solve for (y - 5,880)/5,880:
  0.05/2 = (y - 5,880)/5,880
  0.025 = (y - 5,880)/5,880
  y - 5,880 = 0.025(5,880)
  y - 5,880 = 147
  y = 6,027
  Answer: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let $x$ be the percent increase from 2012 to 2013.
  Let $y$ be the percent increase from 2013 to 2014.
  The number of subscriptions sold in 2013 is 5,880.
  The percent increase from 2013 to 2014 is $y$.
  We want to find the number of subscriptions sold in 2014.
Solution:
  Let $P_1$ be the number of subscriptions sold in 2012 and $P_2$ be the number of subscriptions sold in 2013. We have $P_1=5600$ and $P_2=5880$. 
  Let $P_3$ be the number of subscriptions sold in 2014. We want to find $P_3$. 
  We know that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is $x$. Therefore, $$P_2=P_1\left(1+\dfrac{x}{100}\right)$$$$5880=5600\left(1+\dfrac{x}{100}\right)$$$$1+\dfrac{x}{100}=\dfrac{5880}{5600}=\dfrac{147}{140}$$
  We know that the percent increase from 2013 to 2014 is $y$. Therefore, $$P_3=P_2\left(1+\dfrac{y}{100}\right)$$
  We know that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014. Therefore, $$2x=y$$
  Substituting $2x$ for $y$, we get $$P_3=P_2\left(1+\dfrac{2x}{100}\right)$$$$P_3=5880\left(1+\dfrac{2x}{100}\right)$$$$P_3=5880+\dfrac{11760x}{100}$$$$P_3=5880+117.6x$$
  We want to find $P_3$. To find $P_3$, we need to find $x$. We have $$1+\dfrac{x}{100}=\dfrac{147}{140}$$$$x=\dfrac{5}{7}$$
  Substituting $\dfrac{5}{7}$ for $x$, we get $$P_3=5880+117.6x$$$$P_3=5880+84=5964$$
  Therefore, the manager expected 5,964 subscriptions to be sold in 2014.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The percent increase from 2012 to 2013 is $\frac{5880-5600}{5600}\times 100\%=5\%$.
  Let $x$ be the number of subscriptions sold in 2014. Then, the percent increase from 2013 to 2014 is $\frac{x-5880}{5880}\times 100\%$.
Action:

Question: A customer paid $\$ 53.00$ for a jacket after a 6 percent sales tax was added. What was the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 47.60$
  B: $\$ 50.00$
  C: $\$ 52.60$
  D: $\$ 52.84$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  A sales tax of 6 percent was added to the price of the jacket.
  Let's call the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added "x".
  To find the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added, we need to solve the equation: $x + 0.06x = 53$
  Simplifying the equation, we get: $1.06x = 53$
  Dividing both sides by 1.06, we get: $x = 50$
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The price of the jacket before the sales tax was added can be found by dividing the total cost (including tax) by the tax rate plus 1.
  The tax rate is 6 percent, which can be written as 0.06.
Action: Answer("B")  
To find the price of the jacket before tax, we can use the formula:
price before tax = total cost / (tax rate + 1)
In this case, the total cost is $\$ 53.00$ and the tax rate is 6 percent or 0.06.
So, price before tax = $\frac{53}{1+0.06} = \$50.00$
Therefore, the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added was $\$ 50.00$. Answer: B.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The total cost of the jacket after tax is $\$ 53.00$. 
  The sales tax is 6%, which means that it is 6/100 times the price of the jacket before tax.
  To determine the price of the jacket before tax, we need to subtract the amount of sales tax from the total cost of the jacket.
Action: 

Let x be the price of the jacket before tax. 

The sales tax is 6% of x, which is 0.06x. 

The total cost of the jacket is the sum of the price before tax and the sales tax: 

x + 0.06x = 1.06x 

We are given that the total cost of the jacket after tax is $\$ 53.00$, so: 

1.06x = 53 

To determine x, we divide both sides by 1.06: 

x = 50 

So, the price of the jacket before the sales tax was added was $\$ 50.00$.

Answer: Answer("B")

  B: $\$ 50.00$ is the closest to the original price, but it is not correct because it does not include the sales tax.

  Therefore, the price of the jacket before tax was $\$ 50.00$.

Question: The world's population has grown at an average rate of 1.9 percent per year since 1945. There were approximately 4 billion people in the world in 1975. Which of the following functions represents the world's population $P$, in billions of people, $t$ years since $1975 ?(1$ billion $=1,000,000,000)$
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=4(1.9)^{t}$
  C: $P(t)=1.19 t+4$
  D: $P(t)=1.019 t+4$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The growth rate of the world population since 1945 is 1.9% per year.
  In 1975, the world's population was approximately 4 billion people.
  
Explanation:
  Since the population grows at a rate of 1.9% per year, we can use the formula for exponential growth: $P(t)=P_{0}(1+r)^{t}$, where $P_{0}$ is the initial population, $r$ is the annual growth rate (as a decimal), and $t$ is the time (in years). 
  
  We know that the initial population in 1975 was 4 billion people, so $P_{0}=4$. The annual growth rate is 1.9%, or 0.019 as a decimal. We want to find the function that represents the world's population $P$, in billions of people, $t$ years since 1975, so we use $t$ as the time variable. 
  
  Putting it all together, we get:
  $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$

Choices:
  A: $4 x^{2} y^{2}$
  B: $8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
  C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$
  D: $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$

&= 2x^{2}y+8xy^{2}-6y^{2}
\end{aligned}
$$

Question: A company purchased a machine valued at $\$ 120,000$. The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year so that after 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$. Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The value of the machine is decreasing linearly over time.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$, and after 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$.
  The slope of the line is $\frac{30,000 - 120,000}{10 - 0} = -9,000$.
  The equation of the line can be written in slope-intercept form as $v = -9,000 t + b$, where $b$ is the $y$-intercept of the line.
  To find $b$, we can use the initial value of the machine, which is $\$ 120,000$.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The machine depreciates by the same amount each year.
  The initial value of the machine is $\$ 120,000$.
  After 10 years, the value of the machine will be $\$ 30,000$.
  We need to find the equation that gives the value of the machine in dollars $t$ years after it was purchased, where $0\leq t\leq 10$.
  
To solve this problem, we can use the point-slope form of the equation of a line, which is:

$y-y_1=m(x-x_1)$

where $m$ is the slope of the line, $x_1$ and $y_1$ are the coordinates of a point on the line.

Let's use the points $(0,120000)$ and $(10,30000)$ to find the slope of the line:

$m=\dfrac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}=\dfrac{30000-120000}{10-0}=-9000$

So the equation of the line is:

$v-120000=-9000(t-0)$

$v=-9000t+120000$

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$Which ordered pair $(x, y)$ satisfies the system of equations shown above?
Choices:
  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
Knowledge: To solve the system of equations, we can substitute $x=y-3$ into the second equation and solve for $y$, then we can find $x$ by using $x=y-3$.
Action: 
Substitute $x=y-3$ into the second equation to get:
$$\frac{y-3}{2}+2y=6$$
Simplify and solve for $y$:
$$\frac{y}{2}+2y=9 \Rightarrow y=\frac{6}{5}$$
Substitute $y=\frac{6}{5}$ into $x=y-3$ to get:
$$x=\frac{6}{5}-3=\frac{-9}{5}$$
So the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $\left(\frac{-9}{5},\frac{6}{5}\right)$.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Solution:
We can start solving the system of equations by substituting the first equation into the second equation and then solving for $y$.
$$\begin{aligned}& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6 \\& \frac{y-3}{2}+2 y=6 \\& 2y-3+4y=12 \\& 6y=15 \\& y=2.5\end{aligned}$$
Now, we can use the value of $y$ to find the value of $x$ using the first equation.
$$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& x=2.5-3 \\& x=-0.5\end{aligned}$$
Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(-0.5,2.5)$.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

Therefore, the ordered pair $(x,y)$ that satisfies the system of equations is $(0,3)$. Answer: $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ (0,3)}$.

  A: Substituting $x=-3$ into the second equation, we get $\frac{-3}{2}+2y=6$. Solving for $y$, we get $y=3$. Plugging $y=3$ back into the first equation, we get $x=0$. So the ordered pair $(x,y)=(-3,0)$ does not satisfy the system of equations.
  B: Substituting $x=0$ into the second equation, we get $2y=6$, which means $y=3$. Plugging $y=3$ back into the first equation, we get $x=0$. So the ordered pair $(x,y)=(0,3)$ satisfies the system of equations.
  C: Substituting $x=6$ into the second equation, we get $3+2y=6$. Solving for $y$, we get $y=\frac{3}{2}$. Plugging $y=\frac{3}{2}$ back into the first equation, we get $x=\frac{3}{2}$. So the ordered pair $(x,y)=(6,-3)$ does not satisfy the system of equations.
  D: Substituting $x=36$ into the second equation, we get $18+2y=6$. Solving for $y$, we get $y=-6$. Plugging $y=-6$ back into the first equation, we get $x=-9$. So the ordered pair $(x,y)=(36,-6)$ does not satisfy the system of equations.

Response 4:
Knowledge:
We can solve for $x$ in the first equation and substitute it into the second equation to get a value for $y$.

$$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \quad \Rightarrow \quad x+3=y \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6 \quad \Rightarrow \quad \frac{x}{2}+2(x+3)=6 \\& \quad \Rightarrow \quad \frac{x}{2}+2x+6=6 \quad \Rightarrow \quad \frac{5x}{2}=-6 \quad \Rightarrow \quad x=-\frac{12}{5}\end{aligned}$$

Topic: Math
Question: Ken is working this summer as part of a crew on a farm. He earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week. Because of his performance, his crew leader raised his salary to $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week. Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week. What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- Ken earned $\$8$ per hour for the first $10$ hours he worked this week.
- His salary was raised to $\$10$ per hour for the rest of the week.
- Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week.
- We need to find the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$270$ for the week.

Let's first find how much Ken earned from the first 10 hours: 
$$10 \text{ hours} \times \$8/\text{hour} = \$80$$
Let $h$ be the number of hours Ken works the rest of the week. Then his total earnings for the week will be:
$$\$80 + (\$10/\text{hour})h$$
Now we need to find the least $h$ such that $90 \%$ of his total earnings is at least $\$270$. So we need to solve the following inequality for $h$:
$$0.9(\$80 + (\$10/\text{hour})h) \geq \$270$$
Simplifying this inequality, we get:
$$h \geq 22$$
So the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$270$ for the week is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ 22}$.

  S &= 0.9E \\
  &= 0.9(80 + 10x) \\
  &= 72 + 9x
  \end{align*}
  We want to find the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week.

  \begin{align*}
  S &\geq 270 \\
  72 + 9x &\geq 270 \\
  9x &\geq 198 \\
  x &\geq 22
  \end{align*}
  Therefore, the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) } 22}$.

Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To maximize the number of 120-pound packages, we need to minimize the number of 100-pound packages.
  Let x be the number of 100-pound packages and y be the number of 120-pound packages.
  We have the following constraints:
  x + y >= 10 (the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages)
  100x + 120y <= 1100 (the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds)
  A: If we take only 120-pound packages, we can carry at most 9 packages (9 x 120 = 1080), which is not enough to meet the minimum requirement of 10 packages.
  B: If we take 4 120-pound packages, we can take 6 100-pound packages to meet the minimum requirement of 10 packages. The total weight of the packages is 4 x 120 + 6 x 100 = 960 + 600 = 1560, which exceeds the maximum weight limit of 1,100 pounds.
  C: If we take 5 120-pound packages, we can take 5 100-pound packages to meet the minimum requirement of 10 packages. The total weight of the packages is 5 x 120 + 5 x 100 = 1200, which is within the weight limit. This is the maximum number of 120-pound packages we can carry.
  D: If we take 6 120-pound packages, we can take 4 100-pound packages to meet the minimum requirement of 10 packages. The total weight of the packages is 6 x 120 + 4 x 100 = 1440 + 400 = 1840, which exceeds the maximum weight limit of 1,100 pounds.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
- The helicopter must carry at least 10 packages per trip.
- The packages can be either 100 or 120 pounds.
- The total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds.

Let x be the number of 100-pound packages and y be the number of 120-pound packages.
Then, we have the following system of inequalities:
10 <= x + y <= 11
100x + 120y <= 1100

We want to maximize y, the number of 120-pound packages.
To do this, we can solve for x in the first inequality and substitute it into the second inequality:
10 - y <= x <= 11 - y
100(10 - y) + 120y <= 1100
1000 - 100y + 120y <= 1100
20y <= 100
y <= 5

Therefore, the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is 5.

Topic: Math
Question: Kathy is a repair technician for a phone company. Each week, she receives a batch of phones that need repairs. The number of phones that she has left to fix at the end of each day can be estimated with the equation $P=108-23 d$, where $P$ is the number of phones left and $d$ is the number of days she has worked that week. What is the meaning of the value 108 in this equation?
Choices:

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 44 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Which of the following complex numbers is equal to $(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right)$, for $i=\sqrt{-1}$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-14-18 i$
  B: $-4-6 i$
  C: $4+6 i$
  D: $14+18 i$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
We know that $i^2=-1$, so we can substitute this value into the expression given in the question and simplify it.
$(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right) = (5+12i) - (9(-1)-6i) = (5+12i)+(9+6i) = 14+18i$
A: $-14-18i$ is not equal to the given expression.
B: $-4-6i$ is not equal to the given expression.
C: $4+6i$ is not equal to the given expression.
D: $14+18i$ is equal to the given expression.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
We know that $i=\sqrt{-1}$ and $i^2=-1$, and we can simplify the given expression by substituting $i^2=-1$ and doing the arithmetic.
$(5+12i) - (9i^2 - 6i) = (5+12i) - (9(-1) - 6i) = 5 + 12i + 9 + 6i = 14 + 18i$
Action: Answer("D")

Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The equation of a parabola in vertex form is $y=a(x-h)^2+k$, where $(h,k)$ is the vertex.
  The vertex of $y=(x-11)^2$ is $(11,0)$.
  The line $y=25$ is a horizontal line.
  The intersection points of the parabola and the line will have the same $y$-coordinate of 25.
  We can solve for the $x$-coordinates of the intersection points by setting $(x-11)^2=25$ and solving for $x$.
Action: 
  $(x-11)^2=25$
  $x-11=\pm5$
  $x=6$ or $x=16$
  The distance between the $x$-coordinates of $A$ and $B$ is $16-6=10$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Townsend Realty purchased the Glenview Street property and received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price along with an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash. Which of the following best approximates the original price, in dollars, of the Glenview Street property?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 350,000$
  B: $\$ 291,700$
  C: $\$ 233,300$
  D: $\$ 175,000$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
Let the original price of the property be $P$. After a $40 \%$ discount, the price becomes $0.6P$. After an additional $20 \%$ discount, the price becomes $0.8(0.6P) = 0.48P$.
A: $\$ 350,000$ is not a possible answer because $0.48P < 0.6P < P$.
B: $\$ 291,700$ is a possible answer because $0.48P$ is approximately equal to a $52 \%$ discount off the original price.
C: $\$ 233,300$ is not a possible answer because $0.48P$ is greater than the $60 \%$ discount off the original price.
D: $\$ 175,000$ is not a possible answer because $0.48P$ is greater than the $80 \%$ discount off the original price.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
Let the original price of the property be $x$ dollars.
Townsend Realty received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price, which means they paid $60 \%$ of the original price.
They also received an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price, which means they paid $80 \%$ of the discounted price.
Thus, the price they paid is $0.8 \times 0.6 x = 0.48x$ dollars.
The original price $x$ can be found by dividing this price by $0.48$.

Action: 
Let's work backwards to find the original price of the property:
\begin{align*}
0.48x &= \text{price Townsend Realty paid} \\
&= \text{discounted price} \times 0.8 \\
&= (0.6x) \times 0.8 \\
&= 0.48x.
\end{align*}
Therefore, the original price of the property was $x = \text{price Townsend Realty paid} / 0.48 = (\text{discounted price} \times 0.8) / 0.48$.

$$
\begin{aligned} 
\frac{0.48x}{0.8 \times 0.6} &= \frac{0.48x}{0.48} \\
&= x
\end{aligned}
$$
Therefore, the original price of the property was approximately $\$233,300$.
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
Let the original price of the Glenview Street property be $x$. 
Townsend Realty received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price, so they paid $0.6x$. 
They also received an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price, which means they paid $0.8(0.6x) = 0.48x$. 
We are asked to find $x$. 

$0.48x$ is $48 \%$ of $x$.

To solve the problem, we can set up the equation:
$$0.48x = x - 0.4x$$
which simplifies to
$$0.08x = x \cdot 0.4$$
Dividing both sides by $0.08$, we get
$$x = \frac{x \cdot 0.4}{0.08} = 5x$$
Action: Answer("C")  
So, the original price of the Glenview Street property was approximately $\$ 233,300$.

  B: $f(x)=3 x+2$
  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$
Response 0:
Knowledge:

  The slope of a line through two points $(x_1,y_1)$ and $(x_2,y_2)$ is $m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
Action: 
  The slope of the line through the points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$ is $m=\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4$.
  Therefore, the equation of the line is $f(x)=4x+b$, where $b$ is the $y$-intercept.
  To find $b$, we can use the point $(1,5)$, which gives $5=4(1)+b$, so $b=1$.
  Thus, $f(x)=4x+1$, which is choice $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}}$.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To define a linear function, we need to find the slope and the $y$-intercept.
  The slope is given by the formula $m=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{f(x_2)-f(x_1)}{x_2-x_1}$.
  Once we have the slope $m$, we can find the $y$-intercept by using the formula $b=f(x_1)-m x_1$ where $(x_1,f(x_1))$ is one of the given points.
  
We can use the given points to find the slope:
  $m=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{f(3)-f(1)}{3-1}=\frac{13-5}{2}=4$.
  
Then, we can use the slope and one of the given points to find the $y$-intercept:
  $b=f(1)-m\cdot 1=5-4=1$.
  
Therefore, the equation of the linear function $f$ is $f(x)=4x+1$.

Question: Which of the following is equivalent to $2 x\left(x^{2}-3 x\right)$ ?
Choices:

  B: $3 x^{3}-x^{2}$

Question: Dreams Recalled during One Week\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|c|c|}\hline& None & 1 to 4 & 5 or more & Total \\\hline\hlineGroup X & 15 & 28 & 57 & 100 \\\hlineGroup Y & 21 & 11 & 68 & 100 \\\hlineTotal & 36 & 39 & 125 & 200 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The data in the table above were produced by a sleep researcher studying the number of dreams people recall when asked to record their dreams for one week. Group X consisted of 100 people who observed early bedtimes, and Group Y consisted of 100 people who observed later bedtimes. If a person is chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream, what is the probability that the person belonged to Group Y ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{68}{100}$
  B: $\frac{79}{100}$
  C: $\frac{79}{164}$
  D: $\frac{164}{200}$
Response 0:
The table above shows the number of people in each group who recalled none, 1 to 4, or 5 or more dreams during the study. To find the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belonged to Group Y, we need to use the following formula:

Probability = (Number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream) / (Total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream)

The number of people in Group Y who recalled at least 1 dream is 11 + 68 = 79. The total number of people who recalled at least 1 dream is 39 + 125 = 164. Therefore, the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belonged to Group Y is:

Probability = 79 / 164

To find the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belongs to Group Y, we need to add the probability that the person recalled 1 to 4 dreams and belongs to Group Y to the probability that the person recalled 5 or more dreams and belongs to Group Y. So, the answer is:

$\frac{11}{39} \cdot \frac{39}{200} + \frac{68}{125} \cdot \frac{125}{200} = \frac{79}{200}$

Therefore, the answer is (B) $\frac{79}{100}$.
Response 8:
The table shows that there are a total of 39 people who recalled 1 to 4 dreams and 125 people who recalled 5 or more dreams. Therefore, there are 39+125=164 people who recalled at least 1 dream. Out of these 164 people, 68 belonged to Group Y. Thus, the probability that a person chosen at random from those who recalled at least 1 dream belonged to Group Y is: 

$$\frac{68}{164}$$

Simplifying this fraction by dividing numerator and denominator by 4, we get:

$$\frac{17}{41}$$

Therefore, the answer is (after simplification): 

$$\frac{17}{41}$$

Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:

    $C_S=75(h+2)+125$ where $C_S$ is the amount charged for Ms. Sanchez's job.
    $C_R=75h+125$ where $C_R$ is the amount charged for Mr. Roland's job.
Action: 
  We need to find the difference between $C_S$ and $C_R$.
  $C_S-C_R=75(h+2)+125-(75h+125)=75h+150-75h=150$
  Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$ 150$ more than Mr. Roland.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 58 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Energy per Gram of Typical Macronutrients.\begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}.\hline.Macronutrient & Food calories & Kilojoules \\.\hline.Protein & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.Fat & 9.0 & 37.7 \\.\hline.Carbohydrate & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.The table above gives the typical amounts of energy per gram, expressed in both food calories and kilojoules, of the three macronutrients in food.
Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The table provides the energy per gram of protein, fat, and carbohydrate in both food calories and kilojoules.
  - The granola bar contains 180 food calories, but we do not know the mass of the granola bar.
  - If the granola bar contains $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, then the total energy in food calories is given by $4p+9f+4c=180$.
Action: 
  We can rearrange the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$ to solve for $f$ and get $f=\frac{180-4p-4c}{9}$. 
  This simplifies to $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$. 
  So the answer is (B). 
  Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The energy per gram of protein is 4.0 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules.
  The energy per gram of fat is 9.0 food calories or 37.7 kilojoules.
  The energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4.0 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules.
  
Let $p$, $f$, and $c$ be the grams of protein, fat, and carbohydrate, respectively, in the 180 calorie granola bar. Then we have the equation $4p+9f+4c=180$ for the total energy in food calories. We want to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.

We can rearrange the equation as $9f=180-4p-4c$, and then divide both sides by 9 to get $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: The energy per gram of protein is 4 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules. The energy per gram of fat is 9 food calories or 37.7 kilojoules. The energy per gram of carbohydrate is 4 food calories or 16.7 kilojoules. 

Let $p_g$ be the amount of energy in food calories that comes from protein per gram, $f_g$ be the amount of energy in food calories that comes from fat per gram, and $c_g$ be the amount of energy in food calories that comes from carbohydrate per gram. Then we have:
$$
\begin{aligned}
180 &= p p_g + f f_g + c c_g \\
&= 4p + 9f + 4c
\end{aligned}
$$
We can solve this equation for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.

$$
\begin{aligned}
180 &= 4p + 9f + 4c \\
9f &= 180 - 4p - 4c \\
f &= 20 - \frac{4}{9}(p+c)
\end{aligned}
$$

Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  - The table provides the energy content per gram of protein, fat, and carbohydrate in food.
  - The problem involves a system of linear equations.
  - We can use the information in the table to set up an equation relating the calories in the granola bar to the amounts of protein, fat, and carbohydrate in the bar.
  - We can then use algebra to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.

Action: 
The total energy in the granola bar comes from the protein, fat, and carbohydrate in the bar. Let $p$, $f$, and $c$ be the number of grams of protein, fat, and carbohydrate, respectively, in the bar. Then we have:
$4p + 9f + 4c = 180$
We can rearrange this equation to solve for $f$:
$9f = 180 - 4p - 4c$
$f = \frac{180 - 4p - 4c}{9}$
$f = \frac{20}{9}(9 - p - c)$
$f = 20 - \frac{4}{9}(p + c)$
Therefore, the answer is (B) $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40 \\.& D(P)=220-P.\end{aligned}.$$.The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are functions of the price of the product. The functions above are the estimated supply and demand functions for a certain product. The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are equal at the market equilibrium price. This means that we need to find the price at which $S(P)=D(P)$.
  $S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40$ is the supply function.
  $D(P)=220-P$ is the demand function.
Action: 
  Equating the supply and demand functions, we get:
  $$\begin{aligned}
  S(P)&=D(P)\\
  \frac{1}{2} P+40&=220-P\\
  \frac{3}{2} P&=180\\
  P&=120
  \end{aligned}$$
  Answer: Answer("B")

$x=10$

Question: $$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$In the equation above, $k$ is a constant. If $x=9$, what is the value of $k$ ?

  A: 1
  B: 7
  C: 16
  D: 79

$$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$$

$$(\sqrt{k+2})^2=x^2$$
$$k+2=x^2$$
$$k=x^2-2$$
$$k=9^2-2$$
$$k=79$$

Response 6:
Knowledge:
We can solve the equation $\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$ for $k$ by isolating the variable $k$.
We start by squaring both sides of the equation to get rid of the square root.
$\sqrt{k+2}-x=0$
$(\sqrt{k+2}-x)^2=0^2$
$k+2-2x\sqrt{k+2}+x^2=0$
Then we move all the terms containing $k$ to one side of the equation and simplify
$k+2-2x\sqrt{k+2}+x^2=0$
$k-2x\sqrt{k+2}=-x^2-2$
$k^2-4x^2k+4x^4= x^4+4x^2+4$
$k^2-4x^2k= x^4+4$
$k(k-4x^2)= x^4+4$
$k=\frac{x^4+4}{k-4x^2}$
Action: Answer("C")

$$k+2-2x\sqrt{k+2}+x^2=0$$
$$k+2-x^2=2x\sqrt{k+2}$$
$$\frac{k+2-x^2}{2x}=\sqrt{k+2}$$
$$\left(\frac{k+2-x^2}{2x}\right)^2=k+2$$
$$\frac{(k+2-x^2)^2}{4x^2}=k+2$$
$$k+2=\frac{(k+2-x^2)^2}{4x^2}$$
$$4x^2(k+2)=(k+2-x^2)^2$$
$$4x^2k+8x^2=k^2+4kx^2+4x^4-2kx^2-4x^2+2k+4$$
$$0=k^2+(2x^2-1)k+(4x^4-4x^2+4)$$
Action: We can plug in the value of $x$ and solve for $k$. 
$$0=k^2+(2x^2-1)k+(4x^4-4x^2+4)$$
$$0=k^2+(2(9)^2-1)k+(4(9)^4-4(9)^2+4)$$
$$0=k^2+161k+1292$$
$$k=\frac{-161\pm\sqrt{(161)^2-4(1)(1292)}}{2(1)}$$
$$k=-4, -157$$
Since $k$ is a constant, the value of $k$ must be unique. Therefore, the answer is:

  We want to find the temperature $t$ that will make the value of $a$ closest to 1,000 feet per second.
  To solve this problem, we can substitute $a=1,000$ into the formula and solve for $t$.

Question: $$2 a x-15=3(x+5)+5(x-1)$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, what is the value of $a$ ?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 2
  C: 4
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve the equation, we need to simplify both sides and then solve for x.
  If no value of x satisfies the equation, then the equation has no solutions.
  If the equation has no solutions, then the coefficients of x on both sides must be equal.
  The coefficient of x on the left side is 2a.
  The coefficient of x on the right side is 3+5=8.
  Therefore, 2a=8, which implies a=4.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To solve the equation, we need to simplify the left side and the right side of the equation and then find the value of $a$ that makes the equation inconsistent, in other words, the value of $a$ that makes the equation have no solution.
Action:

$$2ax-15=3x+15+5x-5$$
$$2ax-15=8x+10$$
$$(2a-8)x=25$$
$$x=\frac{25}{2a-8}$$
If no value of $x$ satisfies the equation, it means that $2a-8$ must be equal to zero, because otherwise we could always find a value of $x$ that satisfies the equation. Therefore:
$$2a-8=0$$
$$a=4$$

Question: The function $f$ is defined by $f(x)=(x+3)(x+1)$. The graph of $f$ in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following intervals contains the $x$-coordinate of the vertex of the graph of $f$ ?

  A: $-4<x<-3$
  B: $-3<x<1$
  C: $1<x<3$
  D: $3<x<4$
Response 0:
Knowledge:

  The vertex of a parabola in the form $f(x) = ax^2 + bx + c$ is located at the point $(-\frac{b}{2a}, f(-\frac{b}{2a}))$.
  The function $f$ can be expanded as $f(x)=x^2 + 4x + 3$.
  The $x$-coordinate of the vertex of a parabola in the form $f(x) = ax^2 + bx + c$ is $-\frac{b}{2a}$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$0.10 x+0.20 y=0.18(x+y)$$Clayton will mix $x$ milliliters of a $10 \%$ by mass saline solution with $y$ milliliters of a $20 \%$ by mass saline solution in order to create an $18 \%$ by mass saline solution. The equation above represents this situation. If Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, how many milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution must he use?
Choices:
  A: 5
  B: 25
  C: 50
  D: 100
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  To solve the equation, we need to distribute the $0.18$ on the right side of the equation:
  $$0.10x+0.20y=0.18x+0.18y$$
  Then, we can simplify the equation by isolating one of the variables, for example:
  $$0.02y=0.08x$$
  $$y=4x$$
  This means that the ratio of $y$ to $x$ is $4:1$.
  
Action: 
  We are told that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the $20 \%$ by mass saline solution, which is $y$ in the equation. Since the ratio of $y$ to $x$ is $4:1$, we can find $x$ by dividing $100$ by $4$, which gives us $25$. Therefore, Clayton must use 25 milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution. 
  Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  To solve for one variable in an equation with two variables, we need another equation.
  In this case, we know that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the 20% saline solution, so the total amount of saline solution used is $x+100$ milliliters.
  We can set up another equation using the fact that the final mixture is 18% saline solution by mass.
Action: We can start by simplifying the equation given:
$$0.10x+0.20y=0.18(x+y)$$
Distribute 0.18 on the right side:
$$0.10x+0.20y=0.18x+0.18y$$
Subtract 0.10x from both sides:
$$0.20y=0.08x+0.18y$$
Subtract 0.18y from both sides:
$$0.02y=0.08x$$
Divide both sides by 0.02:
$$y=4x$$
We know that Clayton uses 100 milliliters of the 20% saline solution, so the total amount of saline solution used is $x+100$ milliliters. We can set up another equation using the fact that the final mixture is 18% saline solution by mass:
$$0.10x+0.20(100)=0.18(x+100)$$
Simplify and solve for x:
$$0.10x+20=0.18x+18$$
$$0.08x=2$$
$$x=25$$
Therefore, Clayton must use 25 milliliters of the 10% by mass saline solution. Answer: \boxed{\textbf{(B) }25}.

  $$0.10 x+20-0.10 x=0.18 x-0.10 x+18$$

  $$20-18=0.08 x$$

  $$2=0.08 x$$

  $$\frac{2}{0.08}=x$$
  Simplify.
  $$25=x$$
  Therefore, Clayton must mix 25 milliliters of the $10 \%$ by mass saline solution.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 6.0 | Problem 73 of 100 ###

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|c|c|c|}\hline\multicolumn{7}{|c|}{Lengths of Fish (in inches)} \\\hline8 & 9 & 9 & 9 & 10 & 10 & 11 \\\hline11 & 12 & 12 & 12 & 12 & 13 & 13 \\\hline13 & 14 & 14 & 15 & 15 & 16 & 24 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above lists the lengths, to the nearest inch, of a random sample of 21 brown bullhead fish. The outlier measurement of 24 inches is an error. Of the mean, median, and range of the values listed, which will change the most if the 24 -inch measurement is removed from the data?
Choices:
  A: Mean
  B: Median
  C: Range
  D: They will all change by the same amount.
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The mean is the sum of all values divided by the number of values.
  The median is the middle value when the values are listed in order.
  The range is the difference between the maximum and minimum values.
  There are 21 values in the data set, and one of them is an outlier value of 24 that needs to be removed.
  The mean is sensitive to outliers because it uses all values in the calculation.
  The median is resistant to outliers because it only uses the middle value(s) in the calculation.
  The range is sensitive to outliers because it uses the maximum and minimum values in the calculation.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Mean is the average value of a set of data.
  Median is the middle value of a set of data when arranged in order.
  Range is the difference between the largest and smallest values in a set of data.
  There are 21 measurements in the data set, and one outlier of 24 inches.
  Removing the outlier will reduce the number of measurements to 20.
  The mean is calculated by summing all the measurements and dividing by the number of measurements.
  The median is calculated by finding the middle value when the measurements are arranged in order.
  The range is calculated by subtracting the smallest measurement from the largest measurement.
Action: Answer("A")

  Range: the difference between the largest and smallest values in a set of numbers.

Question: In planning maintenance for a city's infrastructure, a civil engineer estimates that, starting from the present, the population of the city will decrease by 10 percent every 20 years. If the present population of the city is 50,000, which of the following expressions represents the engineer's estimate of the population of the city $t$ years from now?
Choices:

  B: $50,000(0.1)^{\frac{t}{20}}$
  C: $50,000(0.9)^{20 t}$
  D: $50,000(0.9)^{\frac{t}{20}}$

  The present population of the city is 50,000.

After 40 years (t = 40), the population will be 45,000(0.9) = 40,500 (a decrease of 10%).
Thus, the population decreases by a factor of 0.9 every 20 years.

Knowledge:
  The population of the city is decreasing by 10% every 20 years.
  The present population of the city is 50,000.

where:
  A is the amount after time t
  A0 is the initial amount
  r is the decay rate
  d is the time it takes for the amount to decay by a factor of 1/e (the "half-life")

In this problem, the decay rate is 10%, so r = 0.1. The time it takes for the population to decay by a factor of 1/e is not given, so we cannot calculate d directly. However, we can use the fact that the population decreases by 10% every 20 years to estimate the value of d. Since 1/e is approximately equal to 0.37, we can say that the population will decrease by a factor of 0.37 after 20 years. Therefore, we can estimate that d is approximately 20 years.

Using the formula for exponential decay, we can write the expression for the population of the city t years from now as:
  $A = 50,000(1-0.1)^{t/20}$

Simplifying this expression, we get:
  $A = 50,000(0.9)^{t/20}$

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangle was altered by increasing its length by 10 percent and decreasing its width by $p$ percent. If these alterations decreased the area of the rectangle by 12 percent, what is the value of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: 12
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 22
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let L be the original length of the rectangle and W be the original width of the rectangle.
  After the alterations, the new length of the rectangle is 1.10L, and the new width of the rectangle is (1 - p/100)W.
  The new area of the rectangle is (1.10L)(1 - p/100)W = 0.88LW, which is 12% less than the original area LW.
  Therefore, 0.88LW = 0.88(L)(W) = 0.88LW - 0.12LW = 0.76LW.
  It follows that 0.88LW = 0.76LW implies 0.12LW = (1.10L)(p/100)W, which simplifies to p = 10.8.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the original length of the rectangle is $l$ and the original width is $w$. 
  Then the original area of the rectangle is $lw$.
  After increasing the length by 10%, the new length is $1.1l$.
  After decreasing the width by $p$%, the new width is $(1-\frac{p}{100})w$.
  Therefore, the new area of the rectangle is $1.1l(1-\frac{p}{100})w$.
  We are given that the new area is 12% less than the original area. 
  So we can write the equation: $lw - 0.12lw = 1.1l(1-\frac{p}{100})w$

Action:
  $lw - 0.12lw = 1.1l(1-\frac{p}{100})w$ can be simplified to $0.88lw = 1.1l(1-\frac{p}{100})w$
  Dividing both sides by $lw$, we get $0.88 = 1.1(1-\frac{p}{100})$
  Solving for $p$, we get $p = \frac{22}{5}$
  This is equivalent to $p = 4.4$
  None of the answer choices match the exact value of $\frac{22}{5}$, but the closest one is Choice (C) 20.

$lw$ = original area of the rectangle
$1.1l(w(1 - p/100))$ = new area of the rectangle
The percent decrease in the area is given by: $\frac{lw - 1.1l(w(1 - p/100))}{lw} = 0.12$

  If the new area is $z$ percent less than the original area, then $z$ can be expressed as $\frac{(100 - z)}{100} = (1 + \frac{x}{100}) \times (1 - \frac{y}{100}) - 1$
  
Let's use this knowledge to solve the problem:

$\frac{(100 - z)}{100} = (1 + \frac{10}{100}) \times (1 - \frac{p}{100}) - 1$
$0.88 = 1.1 \times (1 - \frac{p}{100}) - 1$
$0.88 = 0.1 - \frac{p}{90}$
$p = (0.1 - 0.88) \times 90$

  B: 6 and 35
  C: 10 and 21
  D: 31 and 41
